I flipped straight there and skimmed---and the name of our prefecture caught my eye. I kept reading.

{\bfseries
\begin{quote}
Since it was deep forest, we had no choice but to walk along the stream, but that stream flowed along the fault and had carved the cliff lined with caves, which made it extremely convenient. From the stream, we could look up at many caves. We climbed up to one of them and tried going in just a little, and then---
\end{quote}
}

This is it. The rest was on the next page. With trembling fingers, I turned to it.

{\bfseries
\begin{quote}
It was clearly still unexcavated. Something that absolutely should not have been left alone had been left there. I won't go into details, but the moment I stepped out of the cave, a distant torii facing this way caught my eye, and I regretted what I'd done---thinking I've done something I shouldn't. When I looked into it later, it seemed to be a restricted area. I don't think I'll ever forget this shocking experience. I can't exactly say it loudly, but this kind of doki-doki is something you can only get by researching on your own.
\end{quote}
}

It was obvious his mouth had slipped---or rather, his pen had. Maybe he'd loosened up while reminiscing because it was a children's book. If someone found this today, it could easily blow up into a scandal.

With everything we'd learned so far in mind, what he was writing about was obvious.
The author had accidentally discovered a sokushinbutsu---or what had become of one.

I was grateful to the author of \textit{Geology and Vegetation of the Tsunanagai City Area} for having the sense to quote this tiny anecdote from a children's book.

``Izuta.''

Without dwelling on it, Hijiri calmly pointed to the edge of the page. I'd been so absorbed in the main text that I hadn't noticed, but there was a note written there in ballpoint pen.


\textbf{Bonus: Find this passage --- 1 point}\\
\textbf{The rest is deeper in, beyond the starting place. How many points do you have, you excellent one?}


``It's a meaningless scribble, but having it on this page feels\dots\ kind of heavy, doesn't it?''

For a while, I couldn't put this feeling into words.
A senpai from ten years ago was speaking to me from the corner of this page.

``It's huge. We hit the jackpot.''

With a slightly trembling hand, I closed the book, took a deep breath to steady myself, and stood up. As I headed toward the checkout counter, Hijiri asked with obvious interest.

``So you've got an idea?''

``Let's go. I want to confirm it while it's still morning.''

Just as we finished checking the book out and were about to leave, the entrance door opened.

Both of us stopped, startled, and looked at each other. It was Kannabi. As she pulled off the headphones covering her ears, she stared at us with wide eyes.

``Eh\dots''

``Good morning, Kannabi-san.''

Hijiri walked right up to Kannabi as if nothing were out of the ordinary, and greeted her cheerfully.

``A light novel.''

``\dots Yeah.''

``I was recommending a little-sister light novel to Izuta. One where they're properly related by blood.''

``Yeah. Did you like it?''

Kannabi's question was directed at me.

``Unfortunately for me, I actually have a little sister, so it doesn't seem like it'd really work for me.''

``You'll know if you read it. It's exactly because you have a real little sister that it'll hit you.''

\textit{What the hell do you know about having a little sister?}

Kannabi stared at Hijiri for a while, then muttered,

``\dots Please, seriously---be careful.''

``Thank you.''

Hijiri nodded to Kannabi, flicked a glance at me, and left the library. Still not knowing what the right response was, I gave Kannabi a small bow and followed after Hijiri.

We found Tokumura-sensei---who had just arrived for work---in the staff room, made up a convenient excuse, borrowed a key, and headed straight for the biology room. Showing would be faster than explaining. I stood in front of the cabinet that held the frog mummy and carefully opened the door. It had a lock, but since I'd checked the contents yesterday, it was already unlocked. Inside, it was packed tight with reserve documents on landslides.

``Can you help me take everything out of here?''

``Of course.''

As I set the plastic case containing the tree frog sokushinbutsu on the table, I explained.

``This is the cabinet Kannabi was talking about. And this is the frog mummy.''

``I see. So this is the `starting place' that message was pointing to.''

``The Shimomura method test starts with this cabinet. I think something's hidden farther back.''

``That `one point'---was it a scoring rubric?''

``Yeah. It was written the same way as Shimomura-senpai's scoring criteria. That's how I knew it was a message from Shimomura-senpai to the Biology Club's kouhai.''

Working in sync, we cleared out the documents in no time.
\textit{The rest is deeper in, beyond the starting place}---so what was hidden in back of this cabinet?

The cabinet was built into the wall, and the back surface was made of white-painted wooden boards. I tried looking through the gaps between the shelves, but I didn't see anything particularly unnatural.

``That's weird. It's just a cabinet.''

``\dots Let's remove the shelves. If something's hidden in the back board, we'll have to take the front off either way.''

Fortunately, the shelves weren't fixed in place---they were only supported by small screws. Hijiri and I removed them one by one.

``Huh?''

When we took off the first one, Hijiri let that slip and peered into the back of the cabinet.

``What is it?''

``There are numbers carved in here. Look.''

In the light of Hijiri's phone, I saw it---on the back-left corner that had been hidden by the shelf board, a small ``1'' had been carved. When I checked the back-right corner, there was a ``2.'' Both numbers had a small round hole punched right through the center.

``Yeah, that's suspicious. Let's take all the shelves out.''

The cabinet had six levels in all, and there were five removable shelf boards. Once we removed them all, just as expected, the second level had ``3'' and ``4,'' the third had ``5'' and ``6,'' and so on---each level had the same kind of numbers with small holes. The last shelf board had ``9'' and ``0'' hidden behind it.

``How many points do you have, you excellent one\dots?''

``The camp investigation score was 92 points, right?''

``Yeah. There were eight points' worth of problems we couldn't solve, so that was effectively the highest possible score. But if you factor in that message from earlier, the final total becomes 93.''

``So\dots\ what do we do?''

``Maybe we try inserting something into the holes for `9' and `3'\dots\ We should have a mounted needle.''

I took two mounted needles from the cabinet where the lab tools were stored. A mounted needle was exactly what it sounded like---a needle attached to a handle, used for dissections and making slides. I handed one of them to Hijiri.

``Put yours into the `3.' I'll do the `9.'''

``Got it.''

``We'll do it at the same time. Three, two, one---''

When I inserted the needle into the hole in the center of the number, it fit perfectly. When it hit the back, there was a click---like it caught on something.

There was a loud \textit{thunk}, and the board at the back of the cabinet came loose. Neither of us had expected it to work this well, and Hijiri and I hurriedly caught the board as it fell.

``Amazing. It's like a treasure hunt.''

``It'd be nice if what comes out is real treasure.''

Beyond the white-painted plywood, I could see another white board behind it. The cabinet's back panel was double-layered. On the back of the plywood that had come off, a single clear file was carefully taped in place.

Hijiri met my eyes as if to confirm, then pulled it off at once.

There wasn't much time until morning homeroom. We put the back board back, replaced the shelves, returned the documents, put the frog mummy back, and shut the cabinet securely---then gathered around the clear file.

The clear file was taped shut. Hijiri carefully peeled the tape away.
Inside were two documents and a single memo. On the memo, in the same handwriting as the message left in the book, a short line was written.

\textbf{Bonus: Accomplish what I couldn't---7 points}

The two documents looked like they'd been created by the prefectural government.
The moment I understood what that meant, I realized I'd finally stepped into forbidden territory.

As I sat through the morning classes, there was no way I could stay calm. My heart kept pounding, and that unpleasantly keyed-up state showed no sign of easing. \textit{Of course it didn't---I'd seen something like that.}

\textit{The question was: why go that far?}

What we'd found were copies of two documents titled ``Notice.'' They were dated Heisei 25---in other words, 2013. They were addressed to the CHOSEI Group's representative, Tsuruo Hajime, and signed by the former governor. The contents were simple: in short, because it was a buried cultural properties site, they were to protect the relevant area---and because it included locations with a high risk of sediment disasters, they were to avoid those---so they were being pressed to revise the megasolar construction plan. Maps of the problem areas were attached, too.

Hijiri and I confirmed it with aerial photos, but the recommendation had been completely ignored. The sokushinbutsu cave, a buried cultural properties site, and Jyagasawa, a sediment-disaster caution area, had been shaved down flat with excavation and fill, then covered over with solar panels.

\textit{Why did they have to be so high-handed?}

As I simmered with anger, Hijiri explained in a flat voice.

``In the end, it was all about yield. Ten years ago, because of the feed-in tariff system, megasolar was a speculative target where, if you built it, you'd almost certainly make a killing. Meanwhile, the purchase price of electricity was dropping year by year. The question was how fast you could build, and how large an area you could cover.''

I wasn't very familiar with it, but the feed-in tariff system was apparently a setup where power companies had to buy electricity generated by renewables like solar at a government-set price. It was a policy meant to increase renewables---whose upfront costs were high---for things like protecting petroleum resources and decarbonization, but it turned into a deal that was too good, and that led to rough, heavy-handed development.

The CHOSEI Group, chasing profit, had pushed the development through by force, ignoring cultural properties and disaster risk.

Even so---how did they get away with ignoring an official recommendation? If you did something like this, you shouldn't be able to avoid some kind of penalty.

``It looks like Tsunanagai City carried out the survey itself. So today, first, we'll contact the city about it.''

Hijiri didn't hesitate---he made the call and secured two after-school appointments. The sheer speed was terrifying. One way or another, after school, Hijiri and I were going straight to Tsunanagai City Hall.

Even at lunch, eating the skimpy bento my dad had packed---with too few mini tomatoes---my brain was spinning uselessly in a way that was almost refreshing. Even Iwama asked me, worried, ``Are you feeling sick?''

Then Kannabi came over and suddenly spoke up.

``Going to the bathroom together---''

``Got it. Go into the hallway first.''

Cutting off that trash lie midstream, I put away my half-eaten bento and joined Kannabi in the hallway.

``No matter how you look at it, `going to the bathroom together' is a transparent excuse.''

``I hadn't even said who yet.''

``Fair.''

\textit{But even if some other guy had been inviting me, wasn't it weird for Kannabi to be the one delivering the message?}

The place Kannabi headed for was a deserted hallway lined with rooms like the home ec classroom. Kannabi slowed a little to walk alongside me, and without stopping, she said,

``Hijiri-kun's kind of weird, isn't he?''

``You really went and set me up with a guy that eccentric.''

``\dots Are you mad?''

Kannabi asked, wearing an unusually cautious look. I slowly shook my head.

``No. If anything, I feel like I might actually get along with him.''

``I thought so.''

``What's that supposed to mean?''

``I'm not saying you're alike, but I think you have something in common at the core.''

While I was still trying to work out what that meant, Kannabi changed the subject.

``I can imagine what's going to happen next.''

\textit{Yeah, of course she could.} Kannabi had been participating in Hijiri's and my investigation up until the night before last. Shimomura-senpai, who'd failed to stop the Bandori mountain protection movement, had tried to convey something about the sokushinbutsu and Jyagasawa---and it was Kannabi, and no one else, who'd noticed that crucial hint and passed it on to Hijiri and me.

She probably understood that we were investigating fraud connected to the megasolar construction, too.

``Hijiri probably had a reason for keeping Kannabi away.''

``Yeah. I think he's trying to protect me---not drag me in.''

``\dots Did something happen before?''

When I finally couldn't hold it in and asked, Kannabi gave a meaningful little smile and lowered her gaze.

``Something stupid. If I said it, it'd give away our relationship, so I won't.''

She was putting a weird amount of weight into it. \textit{Whatever. I wasn't that interested in their relationship.}

``Don't worry too much. We're not doing anything wrong.''

``Good. I'm glad.''

After a brief hesitation, Kannabi spoke again.

``But be careful. Hijiri-kun's goodness can go too far sometimes.''

``That sounds like you've got a specific example.''

``I do. In middle school, he pushed two male students who were messing with an unremarkable girl all the way to family court. Even though that girl bore her own share of fault.''

``\dots If they did something criminal, that's on them.''

``Things that would normally have been overlooked---he turned them into a big deal, made them into an incident. Hijiri-kun is that kind of person. He believes in absolute justice, and with that intense light, he'll shamelessly shine it even into places where maybe it doesn't need to shine.''

``I don't really think that's a bad thing, though.''

``You said it, didn't you? Delta and Hijiri-kun have something in common at the core.''

When I tried to argue back, Kannabi cut me off in a sharper tone than usual.

``The light of justice---of course it's better if it shines into every corner of the world. But the fact that there are places no one tries to shine a light into\dots\ means there are reasons for it.''

One of the boys who got sent to family court---apparently, while he was on probation at his new school, he got involved with drugs and ended up in juvenile detention.

\textit{I still thought that was his own karma coming back on him, but I didn't say it out loud.}

\textit{Places no one tries to shine a light into---I could think of too many.}

``In this case, I'm the one who pushed Hijiri-kun. If I hadn't shown interest in Oku Tsunanagai being so suspicious\dots\ if I hadn't told Delta and Hijiri-kun about Shimomura-senpai's setup\dots\ maybe I could've kept you two from going somewhere dangerous.''

Kannabi sounded like she was trying to keep her voice even, but it still trembled.

``But I'm not in a position to do anything about Hijiri-kun anymore. I won't tell you to stop what you're doing, so please---I'm begging you---stay with him, so he doesn't end up getting hurt.''

The interviews at city hall ended in a whimper.

The head of the Construction Division, who we asked about Jyagasawa's danger, kept repeating, ``That's handled by the prefecture, so we can't answer in detail.'' And the head of the Social Education Division, who we asked about buried cultural properties, wouldn't say anything beyond, ``The person in charge at the time isn't here, so we can't answer immediately.'' In the end, they even sent us away without returning the documents, saying, ``We'll take these into our custody.''

``We're high schoolers, so\dots\ it's not like we can blame them for looking down on us.''

As we headed toward Tsunanagai Station, Hijiri said it as calmly as ever.

``Good thing we handed them copies.''

I pulled the clear file out of my bag. The original documents were inside. We'd made copies that morning using the old, small multifunction printer in the biology room. According to Hijiri, using the school's big multifunction machines would leave a log, and there was a risk the contents could leak. The home-use printer that had been sitting dormant in the biology room didn't have that kind of function---(we did need to replace the ink, but) we were able to duplicate them safely.

``Izuta's caution paid off. Let's make the next move.''

We arrived at the station and looked for an empty coin locker. We put the clear file inside, locked it securely, then crossed the pedestrian overpass to the other side of the tracks.

Hijiri had suggested we go to the sea.

The wide beach had clear sightlines, and the sound of the waves was perfect for drowning out voices. We didn't need to worry about eavesdropping. As we walked along the shoreline, Hijiri said lazily,

``If we're unlucky, people who want this problem hidden may already have gotten wind of what we're doing.''

``Probably. City hall's response was honestly pretty suspicious.''

``From here on out, speed is what matters. Tomorrow's Constitution Memorial Day---what's your schedule, Izuta?''

``Nothing in particular.''

``Actually, tomorrow there's a prefecture-sponsored concert in Ebiwakagawa, and apparently the governor is coming.''

``The governor\dots\ you mean the prefectural governor?''

``You thought I meant the metropolitan governor?''

Hijiri smiled mildly and went on.

``My father's junior is the deputy governor right now. Through him, I got us an appointment.''

``An appointment---don't tell me\dots\ with the prefectural governor?''

``Not the metropolitan governor. It's on the condition that we only get a few minutes after the concert. I even managed to secure tickets. Interested in Dvo\v{r}\'ak?''

All I could do was stand there, stunned. Calling city hall was one thing---but he'd somehow set up a meeting with the prefectural governor directly, and he'd done it without me even realizing.

``When did you even set that up?''

``This morning, I called and checked. Then just now, it was finalized over SMS. I wasn't expecting much from city hall, so I put a precaution in place.''

``As expected of you.''

I sounded numb---too tired to be properly surprised---but I meant it from the bottom of my heart.

``I'm not that interested in Dvo\v{r}\'ak, but if you're going, Hijiri, I'll come with.''

``Thank you. It might feel like I'm making a big deal out of it, but we won't get anywhere by digging around at city hall. Even the prefectural government office seems\dots\ questionable. Luckily, the governor's changed since ten years ago, and it's a different faction. If this is a stain left by the previous governor, then we can at least hope the current one will set it right.''

``\dots We probably shouldn't tell anyone we're meeting the governor.''

``Yeah. It'd help if you could tell your family a convenient lie. Tomorrow, come in uniform---might be a bit warm, but I'd be happy if you wore your tie properly, too.''

Just then, my phone vibrated in my pocket. I had notifications turned off for everything except calls. When I took it out, the screen showed: \textit{Vice-principal Nihitsu}.

When I showed it to Hijiri, he nodded.

``Can you answer? No matter what he says, don't let any information slip from our side.''

I nodded and answered. I put it on speaker so Hijiri could hear too.

【Ah, hello---am I speaking to Izuta-san?】

There was no particular sense of urgency; it was the same gentle Kansai dialect he'd used when I'd met him before.
But the fact that he'd called at all was, in itself, proof---more real than anything---that it was urgent.

``Yes, this is Izuta.''

【It's not like I'm scolding you or anything, so I'd like you to relax and listen, but\dots\ I just got an inquiry from city hall. So---what exactly are your students doing research on? Do you have any idea what they might be referring to?】

``During the camp, I got interested, so I've been personally looking into the legends of Oku Tsunanagai.''

【Legends, huh. For that, it sure sounds like you're carrying around some pretty dangerous things.】

I exchanged a look with Hijiri. \textit{The vice-principal already seemed to know.}

``Dangerous---as in what, specifically?''

【Documents suspected of being fabricated. I'm not saying they're completely fake, mind you, but\dots\ it's dangerous. If you do this wrong, it turns into slander, you know. If they file a lawsuit, that's the last thing we need. As far as I'm concerned, I want to get this settled before either of you ends up in danger.】

\textit{The vice-principal said ``either of you.'' Of course he knew I was moving with Hijiri too.}

``When you say `get it settled,' what do you mean?''

【If you'll just stop for now, that's enough. Let me hold onto it for the time being. This isn't something high schoolers can handle. We'll go through proper channels, get everything prepared, and then---if it's really necessary---we'll do it right, together.】

\textit{I remembered what Hongo-senpai had said. The vice-principal's favorite line---``Let me hold onto it''---meant ``absolutely not.'' The phrasing was gentle, but the message was: don't touch this anymore.}

【Don't misunderstand me, all right? I'm on your side, Izuta-san. I'm trying to protect you two right now. That's the one thing I need you to understand.】

``Thank you. Understood. We'll leave it to you, sir.''

【You mean it? Then come see me early after the holiday. I'm usually in the staff room. Until then, you must not do anything, okay?】

``I understand. Thank you in advance.''

【All right. I'm counting on you.】

The call ended. Hijiri shrugged.

``This is a problem. If Izuta backs off, I'll have to do it alone.''

``As if I'm backing off. It's not like we're going to spread it to the media. If all we do is bring the suspicion to the governor's ears, that's a legitimate action. I'm not going to make you fight alone.''

``Thank you. That's incredibly reassuring. I'll take full responsibility. I want you to feel safe with me.''

``Appreciated.''

\textit{Honestly, it took a lot of courage to go against a teacher's warning. But this was still better than letting Hijiri charge in by himself. Kannabi had asked me too.}

``Still, I'm sure that was just a threat---but we should properly check the `possible fabrication' angle. If even one odd point is in there, it could shake the credibility of the whole allegation.''

``Yeah. I don't want to believe Shimomura-senpai would make a mistake like that, but you're right---we need to scrutinize it.''

Hijiri stared out at the sea for a moment, thinking, then turned back to me.

``This is sudden, and it's a forward thing to ask, but---I have one request.''

``What is it?''

``Could you let me stay over at your place tonight, Izuta?''

``At my place? Why?''

``If we're going to scrutinize the documents, we need to finish before tomorrow's concert ends. And in terms of safety too\dots\ being together would be a lot more reassuring. No one will be at my house until tomorrow afternoon.''

``Safety, huh---talk about dramatic. But it wasn't something I needed to refuse, either.''

``Fine. I'll talk to my family.''

Hijiri's ``safety'' talk got real almost immediately.

When we passed through the station on the way home, the coin locker where we'd stored the clear file had been neatly broken open. The metal part of the lock was cleanly severed.

The clear file was gone. In its place, a bare pocketknife had been left behind.

Hijiri immediately pulled out a handkerchief, picked up the knife through the fabric, and held it away from me while he studied the blade closely.

``There's a lot of chipping. Maybe they used this to break the lock.''

``Can you even cut metal with something like that?''

\textit{Even as I wondered, my attention kept flicking behind us. Was someone still watching us in this crowd right now? The thought that we'd been tailed by someone willing to break the law sent a chill down my spine. I didn't know who did it, but they were moving far faster than I'd imagined.}

After filing the necessary reports with the railway company and the nearby police box, we decided to stick to crowded places as much as possible. We leapt onto a route bus just as it was about to depart and sat all the way in the back.

``Do you have any self-defense training?''

Hijiri asked in his usual tone.

``I'm known for playing dead really well---and for running fast.''

``I see. I've dabbled in judo, kendo, and a bit of restraining techniques. It's amateur stuff, but it should buy time. If anything happens, run without hesitation.''

``\dots It won't come to that.''

``Sure. I think the locker thing was just a threat. They don't want this to become a big incident either. But we should be prepared for something like a snatch-and-grab, at least.''

\textit{Ever since we visited city hall, nothing about what was happening---or what we were doing---had felt real. It was like I'd wandered into a movie or TV drama.}

Just to be safe, we got off at a bus stop a little way from the Izuta house. Using my familiarity with the area, I took us along a route that would make it impossible for anyone tailing us to keep us in sight, and we made it home without incident.

When we stopped in front of the gate leading to the front door, the motion sensor tripped, and a bright light shone down on us.

``Is that security camera real?''

Hijiri pointed toward the light.

I could see it: the lens surrounded by LEDs.

``Yeah. The recordings are saved to the cloud.''

``Nice.''

That was all Hijiri said before he flicked his gaze around and stepped through the gate I'd opened.

My parents welcomed our sudden visitor, and even Asahi---who was usually weird about my relationship with girls---didn't get suspicious about my relationship with Hijiri.

That said, Hijiri had said something like, ``Your little sister is suuuper cute,'' so I'd given him a light warning: ``If you look at my sister funny, I'll kill you in the most cruel way I can possibly think of.''

After dinner, I warned Asahi never to come in here (she gave me a slightly suspicious look), and Hijiri and I shut ourselves in my room. We were going to get ready for tomorrow together.

\textit{Should I say I was keyed up, or that I was being stubborn? Either way, I wasn't sleepy at all. The thought of some faceless enemy---someone who erased place names from maps, punched holes in books, and pried open coin lockers---didn't fill me with fear so much as it lit a fire in me: like hell I'd let them win.}

The clear file we'd put in the locker was, of course, empty. It was a diversion tactic we'd set up in case there really was someone out there after our materials. The idea was that if there was some bastard who wanted those documents badly enough, they'd gamble even on the slim chance we'd do something as stupid as store important paperwork in a coin locker---and we'd set the trap to see how they moved.

I'd tried it thinking maybe it'd serve as insurance, but it had worked beautifully. \textit{I didn't know who they were, but whoever was trying to stop us seemed pretty panicked.}

Of course, we'd kept the original documents with us the whole time, and we'd made countless copies---and we even had photos saved in the cloud. In case we were rendered unable to act, we'd also set it so that tomorrow night an email with the photos attached would automatically be sent to the vice governor. No loose ends.

We had a mountain of things we needed to do for tomorrow.

First, we had to compile what we'd learned so far into briefing materials for the governor---keeping it as simple as possible, but not leaving anything out. (``Briefing materials'' was Hijiri's term. It probably meant something like lecture materials.) Hijiri handled the information about Jagasawa, I handled the information about the sokushinbutsu and Shimomura-senpai, and Hijiri pulled it all together into a single document.

And that wasn't all. The document Shimomura-senpai had entrusted to us was a copy, and there was a chance it had been altered along the way. There was even a possibility it had been forged from the ground up. We had to scrutinize just how reliable the information really was.

Using the internet and the information from the books we'd copied so far, Hijiri and I examined the two sheets Shimomura-senpai had left us as critically as we could. Between how little information we had and how hard it was to prove the absence of error, no amount of time felt like enough.

But in the process, something became clear.

The Bandori Mountain conservation movement did seem to have existed up until ten years ago. When I searched persistently, I was able to confirm a few traces of it---but there was an unnaturally small amount of concrete information online. It was only after digging through things like social media that we could finally turn up fragments. It was hard to believe anything other than that some kind of bias had filtered the information out.

Also, in the city meeting minutes, Hijiri found that fifteen years ago there'd been an illegal dumping incident involving industrial waste at a residential development the CHOSEI Group had created elsewhere in the city. The record was littered with ominous phrases: the group representative, Tsurunama, talking about ``claims for damages,'' ``repeated strong protests,'' and the like.

``Maybe the city got cowed by that, and couldn't take a hard line on the megasolar project,''

Hijiri analyzed, sitting cross-legged on my bedroom floor with a cup of coffee in hand.

\textit{The more we investigated, the more the swamp we were stepping into---had already stepped into---started to feel dangerous. In the first place, ten years ago, why had Shimomura-senpai been unable to do what we were about to do, even after gathering so much evidence? Why had the vice-principal been so flustered as he tried to restrain us?}

Catching Hijiri in the brief moment his terrifyingly fast typing paused as he added the new information to the briefing materials, I spoke carefully.

``I'm only saying this just in case\dots\ but even now, you can still stop.''

Hijiri lifted his face from the PC screen and waited for me to continue.

``There's no need to rush and force a conclusion right now. We could prepare more, and it wouldn't be too late to get help from other people. Mikage-senpai, the student council president, might be able to help.''

``No. That won't do. We can't trust Mikage-senpai or Hongo-senpai.''

Hijiri dismissed it instantly. \textit{Was there some reason for that?} I looked at him, but he used a sip of coffee as an excuse to change the subject.

``The more people we have, the slower we'll move. Someone wants to stop us. They're pulling strings to keep information hidden. If we---who know the truth---stop here and now, the threats might go on forever. But if we settle it tomorrow, there'll be no point in threatening us anymore.''

``I understand that. But there's no guarantee there won't be retaliation.''

``Are you scared? It's fine. We're overwhelmingly on the side of justice. I'll protect Izuta---and your precious little sister---even if it costs me my life.''

It was an over-the-top expression, but he seemed to mean it.

``\dots I'm not scared. I just thought there might be someone who'd worry about you, Hijiri.''

``If there's someone out there who worries about me, then they're the kind of person who knows---deep down---that I'll never stop.''

\textit{Someone's face floated into my mind. So the two of them really do understand each other, huh.}

``I get it. What I said earlier wasn't a warning---I was just checking the possibility. Don't worry about it. And it's not like I got cold feet either.''

``Of course. I understand.''

Hijiri said that, then smiled.

``\dots By the way, this is pure curiosity, but why are you going this far, Hijiri? Wanting what's right is admirable, but there were plenty of ways you could've avoided getting this deeply involved, too.''

``That's an interesting question. I've never really stopped to think about it. And I'm guessing an answer like `Because it's obviously better to be right' wouldn't satisfy you.''

``I know it's better to be right than wrong.''

Hijiri thought for a moment, then said,

``If I interpret Izuta's question as `Why me,' then I can at least come up with an answer. Because I can.''

``Isn't it something anyone could do if they decided to?''

``Maybe. But I'm sure most people can't bring themselves to decide. There are lots of people out there who are barely managing to live normally. But I've been blessed---with my environment and my ability---and I've got power to spare. If someone has to seek what's right, then it should be people like us.''

``Did a venomous spider bite you or something?''

``Hahaha. Kannabi-san once said something like that to me, too.''

Then Hijiri turned his eyes---wide, maybe from the caffeine---toward me.

``I won't look away until every bit of darkness reflected in these eyes has been illuminated. If you feel like you can't keep up, tell me any time. I'm not going to force you to keep fighting alongside me.''

\textit{Impressed that he could say something straight out of a superhero movie with a straight face,} I shook my head.

``You'd feel uneasy alone, wouldn't you? I'll stick with you as far as I can.''

I shrugged, and Hijiri cheerfully held out his hand for a handshake.

Before I knew it, the sun was up. It was a nice day. We kept examining the information until our departure time, and we concluded that at the very least, there didn't seem to be any contradictions between what was written in the documents and what was publicly available.

The concert started at 14:00. I casually told Asahi to stay home with our parents today, and we decided to leave the house at 12:00. The travel time was supposed to be a little under an hour, but since we had no idea what might happen, we'd planned to leave early.

Right at noon, we heard an engine outside, and when Hijiri nodded, we stepped out through the front door. A black SUV was parked in front of the gate. A Land Cruiser. Its sturdy-looking body---built for ``Go anywhere, and make it back alive''---felt reassuring, given the situation.

``Get in. We're leaving right away.''

Hijiri put a hand on my back and, for some reason, nudged me a little forcefully into the back seat.

Was it just my imagination? At that moment, out of the corner of my eye, I saw Hijiri's leather shoe flick something red-stained and furry---a lump that looked like the corpse of a sewer rat to me---under the car in a sweeping motion.

I asked Hijiri as he climbed in after me,

``What was that just now---roadkill?''

``Who knows. Maybe a kite dropped it by accident.''

Hijiri said that calmly and shut the door, and I felt a little relieved.
\textit{Because it had looked like there were two dead rats lying in the pool of blood.}

In the driver's seat, Hijiri's father sat in a white polo shirt. When we got in the back, he started the car with only a brief greeting. There was something about his back that didn't feel like an ordinary person's.

``Take a route on back roads that's hard to predict, and get us to the venue. And I don't need to say it, but obey the traffic rules.''

At Hijiri's request, his father silently nodded.

The car headed for the concert venue by roads I didn't recognize. Last night, Hijiri had joked, ``It's the first day of a long weekend, so we'll take the back roads. If it looks like someone's going to interfere, be ready for a car chase,'' but in the end, nothing like that happened, and we arrived at the hall.

Unfortunately, I barely remembered anything about Dvo\v{r}\'ak. Hijiri seemed to have stayed awake the whole time, but the moment I sat down, sleepiness hit me. \textit{I felt I'd done something I should apologize for.}

After the performance, we met the governor in an official car. Hijiri did almost all the talking, so all I did was explain the sokushinbutsu and Shimomura-senpai matters, sticking to the briefing materials. After Hijiri handed the original documents over to the governor, we were dropped off at the rotary at Ebiwakagawa Station.

``It'll be too late once someone's dead. We'll move forward with a re-investigation at the prefectural level.''

As the governor said that and shook Hijiri's hand, I watched, feeling like I was half dreaming.


% ==============================
%        Fragment
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Fragment\\
    Dolus Eventualis
\end{center}
\label{sec:fragDolus}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Fragment}
\vspace{1cm}

\textit{Hijiri-kun was the only person I could call a friend.}

\textit{I'm overly logical, and I'm bad at talking to people. If it were just one or the other, I might still be able to avoid becoming a lost cause, but since it's both, it's hopeless. I say things I don't need to say, the conversation falls apart, I analyze the cause forever, I start to hate talking, I get even worse at it---a negative spiral.}

\textit{The only people who can become friends with me are people who are just as logical as I am, who have enough communication skill to cover for me, and who are generous on top of that.}

At Sunamizu Middle School, the only person like that was Hijiri-kun.

So if it weren't for that unfortunate---and fortunate---accident where I ended up sneaking a look at Hijiri-kun's light novel in the student council room, I probably would've graduated middle school without ever becoming friends with anyone.

Hijiri-kun wasn't an idiot who would say something like, ``Kannabi-san, do you not have any other friends?'' but I'm certain he thought it to himself.

Which is why the message in the congratulatory email he sent me for getting accepted was extremely simple.

\textit{Join some club and make other friends.}

So I decided I'd try to get close with the girl named Iwama Rio, who was the first person to talk to me in class. \textit{Rio fit the criteria for someone who could probably be friends with me.}

The first time I talked with Rio one-on-one was in our first PE class, a few days after entering school. When we paired up in roster order, it turned out I'd be paired with Rio, who was one number away from me.

During class, we only exchanged safe, noncommittal lines, but at lunch, Rio came over to my seat. ``I lent my seat to Mizasaki-kun, so can I sit next to you, Kannabi-san?'' was what she said.

It was Rio---the popular one, the kind of person who'd get chosen as class rep---who spoke to me first, not me, the plainest person in class. As we chatted with Rio leading the conversation, I felt that familiar, indulgent comfort I'd always felt in conversations with Hijiri-kun.

\textit{Her word choices---aimed at precise communication---her careful precautions, and her sincerity in explaining things ahead of time so there'd be no misunderstanding made me feel like I could have a normal conversation if it was with Rio.}

\textit{Looking back, that explanation---``I lent my seat to Mizasaki-kun (who?)''---was probably a way of shutting down any baseless suspicion on my part like, She came to talk to me because she couldn't bear to see me alone. I liked that thoroughly thought-out, honor-student way of thinking---even down to that level.}

The next week, after school---even when I'd been thinking I might stop by a bookstore on the way home, Rio called out to me.

``Hey, Rei, are you heading home already today?''

I turned back and nodded honestly. Then Rio gave me a smile that looked like cherry blossoms in bloom.

``Then, want to walk home together?''

In our conversations so far, we'd already ended up talking about where we lived, so it was established that I was from Sunamizu in the neighboring town, while Rio was from Ebiwakagawa farther beyond that. The road to Tsunanagai Station and the train to Sunamizu Station were the same.

``Um, I was thinking I'd stop by a bookstore, but if that's still okay\dots''

The moment I said it, I regretted it. \textit{I didn't need to be that honest. A bookstore could be another day.}

``Wait, is it the new bookstore that opened in the Central Shopping Street?''

I'd never heard of a bookstore like that, but it must have been a topic of conversation. \textit{Figuring there was no point in showing off more troublesome honesty here,} I nodded once.

``I wanted to go too! Let's go together!''

And just like that, I ended up making a detour---alone with the class's popular girl.

New-student recruitment had already started. Walking side by side with Rio toward the school gate, the number of people calling out to us was clearly different from when I was alone.

``Wanna play badminton with us? Beginners totally welcome!''

``Hey, are you guys interested in being managers? The soccer club has a lot of handsome guys!''

``Come check out band! You'd totally be good at an instrument! You've got that kind of face!''

\textit{So this was the world popular people saw, huh}---I walked along feeling like I was on a social studies field trip. Each time, Rio turned them down with an apologetic look, and kept our pointless conversation going anyway.

\textit{I even found myself thinking: Should I be paying money for this?}

The bookstore in the Central Shopping Street really was new---and it was crowded. I spotted a few Tsunanagai High School students, too. I even saw a first-year with bleached blond hair who looked like he wouldn't study at all, staring seriously at the physics shelf, and I couldn't help being impressed. \textit{As expected of Tsunanagai High School.}

As for Rio, I wondered what she was here for, but she headed straight into the aisle where that blond-haired boy was.

``Whoa, this selection is amazing!''

The shelves she was looking at, excitement in her voice even as she tried to keep it down, were lined with biology books from specialized texts to general-audience ones. Plants and fungi, animals, anthropology, biotechnology---within biology, the categories were divided down even further. It really was an astonishingly robust selection.

``Are you interested in biology, Rio?''

When I asked, Rio nodded twice.

``Yeah. I mean, I'm interested in science in general, but compared to physics or math, I'm better at stuff like biology and kagaku.'' \textit{She seemed to mean chemistry.} ``There's less abstract stuff.''

\textit{I could relate, to a point. I was aiming for the science track because I liked analyzing the world logically, but once it got into complex, abstract formulas, my interest and ability fell short.}

``I'm the same. Even though I'm aiming for the science track, physics and math were my worst scores on the mock exam.''

``But you still got into Tsunanagai High School, so weren't your other subjects amazing?''

``I just hope I can keep saying the same thing at this school.''

The moment I said that, I regretted it. \textit{It was absolutely an unnecessary jab. What was I going to do if I made things awkward for someone this straightforward?}

But that worry was needless. Rio responded with a smile.

``I think you'll be fine if you think about your subject choices. Even if you're science track, if you choose chemistry and biology, you won't have to use physics for entrance exams. That's what I'm planning too.''

\textit{Reading Hijiri-kun's message had prompted me to look into subject selection as well.}

In the science track, you choose two subjects from the four science subjects: physics, chemistry, biology, and earth science. Most people choose physics and chemistry, but if you're thinking about biology, agriculture, medicine, or pharmacy in the future, you might choose biology and pair it with chemistry, which is close as a field. Earth science is technically an option too, but not many people choose it, since there are fewer universities that use it for entrance exams, and high schools and cram schools don't emphasize it much.

\textit{In my case, it wasn't that I was especially interested in biology, but if I had to choose, it would probably be chemistry and biology. Solving biology problems was kind of like reading a mystery, and it was pretty fun.}

After that, we ended up chatting in front of the biology shelves for nearly thirty minutes.

Rio was weirdly knowledgeable about the giant winter moth---apparently it's a moth---and she could recite things about natural toxins that made me think, \textit{Is this really the kind of thing an ordinary person is allowed to know?} Every time she opened a book, she'd talk about this and that with a wealth of knowledge.

\textit{Feeling oddly nostalgic, I realized I'd started to like Rio before I knew it.}

\textit{A popular honor-student type who normally should've been completely out of my reach.}

The books weren't cheap, but we each bought one that looked interesting, promised to swap after we finished reading, and then headed home for the day.

The one I bought was \textit{Learning How to Live with Poison and Spines from 50 Harmful Creatures.}

\textit{Looking back, maybe that day was the first step toward me thinking I might join the Biology Club together with Rio.}

In the end, I joined the Biology Club. There were some circumstances, and I went ahead of her.

It took a lot of courage to show my face at a Biology Club I'd been told had only two boys, but thanks to Mizasaki-kun---the person Rio had lent her seat to---handling things well, I somehow made it through.

Of course, I was alone on the way home that day. \textit{They didn't seem like bad people, but I didn't feel like I could handle walking home with two boys I'd only just met.} As I stepped out through the school gate, I put the wireless headphones that had been hanging around my neck onto my ears.

``Oh---Kannabi-san.''

Someone called out to me. A familiar voice.

``\dots Hijiri-kun.''

A tall boy with slicked-back hair stood there looking at me, the sky behind him turning the color of sunset. The Tsunanagai High School uniform---sharp and elite-looking---suited him well. \textit{And realizing I'd thought that, I understood this was the first time I'd seen Hijiri-kun since our middle school graduation ceremony.}

I hurriedly took my headphones off and hooked them around my arm.

``Kannabi-san, have you picked a club yet?''

Hijiri-kun asked as if making casual conversation.

``\dots Huh? Ah, yeah. Biology Club. I decided to try joining the Biology Club.''

Hijiri-kun looked away slightly.

``I see. That's good. I still can't decide.''

\textit{If we dawdled around in front of the gate, I thought the two boys I'd left in the biology room might catch up.}

``Are you heading home now?''

When I asked, Hijiri-kun nodded without looking at me.

``I was just about to head home. Since we're here, want to go together?''

I nodded and put my headphones away in my backpack.

The two of us walked down the tree-lined road stretching out from the school gate. \textit{The trees still had no leaves---maybe they were ginkgo?}

``Did you go check out any clubs today?''

When I tossed out what should've been a harmless topic, Hijiri-kun hesitated a little.

``\dots Today, I didn't.''

It was already close to five.

``I see.''

When I looked at Hijiri-kun, he looked away again. Hijiri-kun turned his face toward the sea beyond the downhill slope.

We kept walking in silence for a while.

``I guess I can't lie to you, Kannabi-san.''

He said it suddenly, partway down the tree-lined road.

``Today, a senpai invited me, so I went to the Physics Club. Even from the perspective of a humanities guy like me, it seemed pretty interesting. I came up with a little joke about physics and law, but I feel like you'd give me a deadpan reaction, Kannabi, so I'll refrain.''

It surprised me that Hijiri-kun had gone to the Physics Club of all places. \textit{But why did he need to hide it?}

``Only the Physics Club?''

``Yeah. After that, I talked for a while with Mikage-senpai, the Physics Club captain, and Hongo-senpai, the Chemistry Club captain.''

``Hongo-senpai---the blond one?''

``Yeah, that one.''

I didn't know who Mikage-senpai was, but I did know Hongo-senpai. The other day, when I was checking the club's activity days outside the biology room, she was the flashy gal who suddenly talked to me. She was also the one who told me Biology Club was meeting today, and that Izuta-kun and Mizasaki-kun---who were in my class---had joined.

``But what would someone from the Chemistry Club want with you, Hijiri-kun?''

``\dots There's something I need to apologize to you for.''

Only then did Hijiri-kun look at me. He let out a long sigh, then continued.

``On the day the results came out, I sent you a message, right? To congratulate you on getting in. Most of it was from the heart. But there was a part I added because someone told me to.''

``I see\dots''

``The club-picking part, and the subject-selection part. Hongo-senpai suggested it to me that day.''

``That day---as in, the day the results came out?''

``Actually, when I went to Tsunanagai High School's cultural festival, I exchanged contact info with her. Just to be clear, it's not like I had any ulterior motives.''

\textit{Well, sure. But the fact that she'd contacted him on the very day the successful applicants were announced made it seem like it must've been urgent. But\dots\ the content of the message to me?}

``At first, I refused, of course. But Hongo-senpai asked me again, saying it would definitely be good for you, Kannabi-san. So in the end, I did what she said. It was basically the same as what I truly wanted to tell you anyway, and it wasn't like she was pushing me to do anything outrageous. That's what I thought.''

``You don't have to apologize for something like that\dots''

``No. This is what you'd call dolus eventualis. I knew my message might end up guiding you, Kannabi-san, and I sent it anyway.''

Maybe to give me time to understand, Hijiri-kun didn't say anything for a while.

\textit{Dolus eventualis---knowing a certain outcome might happen, and still taking the action that causes it. It was similar to ``secret love,'' but not the same.}

`---Come to think of it, you're planning to go science track, right, Kannabi-san?'

`---You said you're bad at physics, but what are you going to do about your science subject choices?'

`---It might be good to start thinking about that kind of thing early.'

\textit{What had been the trigger that got me and Rio fired up talking about biology?}

`---Sounds like Tsunanagai High School is big on clubs too.'

`---If you find something that feels right, you should definitely join.'

`---I think being challenged by excellent peers could be the chance you need to grow a lot.'

\textit{Why had I decided I wanted to join the Biology Club together with Rio?}

\textit{Both for the same reason: because I'd received that message from Hijiri-kun.}

``I only cooperated because I wanted you to have a fun high school life, Kannabi-san. I never wanted to lead you into joining the clubs the upperclassmen wanted. That wasn't my intent.''

He sounded like he truly regretted it.

``Actually, I'd already heard from Hongo-senpai that you joined the Biology Club. She said something carefree like, `Thanks for giving her a push,' but it didn't make me feel good. This kind of manipulating approach is wrong after all. I'm sorry\dots\ I really am.''

\textit{I felt like I'd been outplayed, but somehow I managed to force the words out.}

``It's not like you did anything wrong, Hijiri-kun. There were other reasons too---why I chose Biology Club.''

``I think so too. Which is why it's more malicious. It's hard to imagine your actions would change just because of one message from me, Kannabi-san. Hongo-senpai probably tried influencing all kinds of people, so she could bring an excellent student like you into the Biology Club when it was on the verge of collapsing. And I got made into an accomplice.''

As Hijiri-kun spoke beside me without hiding his indignation, I was confused about something else.

\textit{I didn't have many people I could call friends. If anyone besides Hijiri-kun had influenced my decisions, it would've been Rio at most. The words that had nudged me into making that grand, almost presumptuous decision---to befriending the class's popular girl---had unquestionably been Hijiri-kun's.}

``If there are other people who sent you similar messages, it might be good to check with them too. Feeding someone similar ideas from multiple directions, indirectly controlling their thinking---if something like that was happening, it'd be practically brainwashing.''

\textit{That's not it, Hijiri-kun.}

``Right. Now that you mention it, maybe there were other messages like that too.''

\textit{I didn't receive messages from anyone but you.}

``But Biology Club seems interesting, so I'm going to keep going. Thank you for worrying about me.''

``If that's the case, then... good. I'll settle things in my own way, too.''

The next day, Hijiri-kun messaged me to say he was joining the Physics Club.

After parting with Hijiri-kun at Sunamizu Station, I kept thinking.

\textit{No matter how much I tried to reason it out, I couldn't explain it.}

\textit{Why had I been influenced this much by a message from a boy I'd only barely read books with in middle school?}

\textit{And how had Hongo-senpai predicted so perfectly that I'd be influenced this much by Hijiri-kun's message---?}


% ==============================
%        Chapter 5
% ==============================
\clearpage
\thispagestyle{plain}
\phantomsection
\begin{center}
    \large\bfseries
    Chapter 5\\
    The Ship and the Wine
\end{center}
\label{sec:ch5V2}
\addcontentsline{toc}{chapter}{Chapter 5}
\vspace{1cm}

The morning after we met with the governor, on Greenery Day, my phone buzzed beside my pillow.

Since we'd ignored the vice-principal's warning, I'd been ready for things to get messy. But when I checked the screen, Iwama's name was there. I hurriedly answered.

``What's up?''

【Ah, um---hello?】

Opening with ``What's up?'' out of nowhere felt awkward. I tried again.

``Sorry. I was kind of half-asleep.''

【It's already noon.】

``I was up late last night. You need something?''

【Um, Del-chan, I just found out, but---】

I pulled the phone a little away from my face and ran my tongue over my lips. \textit{What had Iwama found out?}

【Tomorrow's your birthday, right?】

``Huh?''

\textit{It was anticlimactic.} Come to think of it, it was.

【Mizasaki-kun told me. It sounds like you celebrate with your family every year at night, but---what do you say? Think you can meet up for lunch?】

``Well\dots\ I don't have anything planned at the moment.''

【Then it's decided! Tomorrow at noon---12:00---at Tsunanagai Station! Got it?】

\textit{Iwama was starting to figure me out, too. When I didn't have plans, I had a bad habit of trotting along whenever someone called, even if they wouldn't tell me why.} But this time, I wanted to confirm something.

``I'm fine, but just so we're clear---Iwama, you're not the only one coming, right?''

【Rei and Mizasaki-kun are coming too, but\dots\ would you have preferred it if it were just me?】

\textit{What was I supposed to do with that? Even if I gave her every benefit of the doubt and actually had preferred it to be just us, there was no way I'd say that out loud.}

``I'm just confirming---for safety. I've had surprise additions a few times.''

【There'll be four of us. See you then!】

After I hung up on Iwama, I opened the curtains. As usual, I could hear crows cawing their heads off. Bright spring sunlight poured in under a blue May sky.
It was so bright I had to squint.

The next day, I left the house with time to spare at 11:30, and someone unexpected was waiting outside.

``Oh, Delta-kun. Fancy seeing you.''

Mechanical pencil in hand, she looked up from a math magazine and over at me---Mikage Aya.

``Doing math in front of someone's house and calling it a coincidence doesn't add up.''

``The third problem was tough, so I was thinking about it on a walk.''

``If I hadn't come out, were you planning to sit there solving problems all day?''

``Happy birthday.''

Caught off guard by the congratulations, I gave a small, awkward bow.

``Every year Delta-kun eats dinner---including Asahi-chan's homemade cake---starting around 18:00 on your birthday. So I figured that if your Biology Club friends were going to ask you out, it would be around lunchtime.''

\textit{So she'd come absurdly prepared, huh.}

``I see. What do you want?''

``About that matter---my brother, who's good at catching oni---Oniyanma, is doing everything he can. So I want you to relax. Things won't get any worse.''

\textit{So it had already made it to the student council president.}

``You came all the way to my house just to tell me that?''

``No. I came to ask one thing.''

Mikage closed the math magazine and looked straight at me with those steady eyes.

``Any information you learned after Wednesday, May 1, carries enormous risk simply to know. So please---make sure people you don't want involved don't find out.''

\textit{Wednesday was the day Hijiri and I left club early and went to the municipal library. She knew that much---so much it went past creepy and back around to impressive.}

``You're weirdly well-informed about what I did, and when.''

When I said it carefully, Mikage stepped closer.

``If this request means nothing, then you can do whatever you want to me. So please---just for now, do as I say.''

\textit{I thought, what kind of way is that to ask, but I could tell she probably wasn't lying.}

``So I can boil you or roast you?''

``Of course. Boil me or roast me---so long as my brother allows it.''

``\dots Understood. I wasn't planning to say anything unnecessary to begin with.''

``Please, Delta-kun.''

After repeating herself once more, Mikage immediately left.

\textit{Even though she had my contact info---and even though I'd never told her where I lived---the fact she'd come to tell me in person meant it must have been incredibly important.}

As I walked toward Tsunanagai Station, I worked out a plan to mislead the three of them.

``Ah, Del-chan!''

Before I even spotted Iwama, I heard her voice in front of the station. I scanned in the direction of the voice for a moment before I finally found her. She was in casual clothes, so I didn't recognize her right away.

``Happy birthday!''

``Yeah, thanks.''

\textit{I didn't have a good midday greeting for a classmate beyond ``sup'' or ``hey,'' so it helped that she'd congratulated me right away.}

Up close, I could tell Iwama had dressed up more than usual. The last time I'd seen her in casual clothes was the Tsunanagai walk Kannabi had planned, so this was only the second time---but she wore a wide-brimmed hat and earrings, and she gave the impression she'd put in more effort than back then. A big picnic basket hung from her arm.

``Are we eating outside?''

When I asked, glancing at the basket, Iwama smiled and nodded.

``Yeah. Okay---let's go.''

\fullpageimage{8.jpg}

\thispagestyle{plain}
\vspace{1cm}

Just as I was about to nod and say, ``Yeah,'' I came to my senses.

``Where are the other two?''

``They've got something to do, so they said we're meeting up there!''

\textit{I'd kind of had a feeling. The crafty bastards.}

Iwama headed inland along the road without crossing the tracks. I felt a little relieved.

``Good. I'm glad it's not the seaside.''

``At first I thought the ocean might be nice, but Mizasaki-kun told me the seaside is insane with black kites.''

``In middle school, he had his cheeseburger snatched right out of his hands when he was trying to eat it.''

``I think he might've said that. So I picked Misohara Hill Park instead. Apparently there are crows in the mountains, but there are hardly any black kites. I wonder why.''

``Because crows and black kites don't get along. They overlap in diet. Apparently both sides love hamburgers.''

``True. You see them fighting sometimes, right? Even though they get along in squid beaks.''

``Is that a joke based on the fact that the beak of a cephalopod is called a `crow-tobi'?''

``It landed? As expected of you, Del-chan.''

Iwama laughed, looking like she was having fun. Walking side by side through the city under the bright midday sun felt very peaceful.

Misohara Hill Park was, as its name suggested, on a hill with a great view. And around here, a ``great view'' naturally meant an ocean view down over the bay, but the sea-and-sky scenery was always beautiful, so it couldn't be helped.

The park was bustling with families who'd decided to spend the back half of Golden Week close to home. The weather was great, and the temperature was perfect. I'd been worried that all the good spots would be filled at lunchtime, but it looked like Mizasaki had arrived early and saved us a place. He waved while filming me and Iwama walking side by side with his phone.

``A video?''

``Relax. I'll send it to you later.''

\textit{I had no desire to see what my face looked like next to Iwama.} Normally I would've said, ``Delete it,'' but with Iwama right there, I just shrugged, like, \textit{Do what you want.} Iwama told Mizasaki, ``Thanks for saving us a spot!'' and set the basket down on the picnic blanket.

Kannabi arrived a little later with coffee and donuts for the four of us from a nearby shop. \textit{I'd been convinced Mizasaki and Kannabi had staggered their timing to leave me alone with Iwama, but it looked like they'd actually been running errands. I apologized to them in my head for suspecting them.}

The only one who hadn't prepared anything was me---I'd assumed we'd be eating at a shop, so I'd only brought my wallet. When I told them, apologetically, Iwama let it slide with, ``It's your birthday, so it's fine!''

\textit{That day, they let everything slide.}

Iwama had brought three kinds of homemade sandwiches. The lettuce in the BLT was so crisp it felt like she'd picked it from a garden that morning; the fluffy egg sandwich used a mustard mayo with an old-school coffee-shop feel that I had no idea how she'd made; and the cross-section of the fruit sandwich was as beautiful as something store-bought. On top of that, the plastic container she opened as a side dish was packed to the limit with mini tomatoes that were unbelievably sweet.

Of the donuts Kannabi bought, only one had ``Happy Birthday'' written in chocolate sauce. Since we'd probably be having cake separately, they'd kept the sweets modest. It went perfectly with the strong coffee.

Mizasaki brought a present he said the three of them had picked out together after school on Wednesday. It was a box small enough to fit in one hand, and when I opened it, it turned out to be a tie pin. Apparently it was handmade by a well-known artisan, with a flying squirrel worked into the design.

\textit{I knew I'd never forget the day---it was a happiness I didn't often get. Even setting Mizasaki aside, Iwama and Kannabi had only known me for a month, and yet I genuinely thought of them as close friends.}

``I figured a plant motif would suit Delta, but when we saw a flying squirrel, the three of us decided instantly. Thank God Delta wasn't there that day---pure luck.''

Nodding along to Mizasaki's explanation, I put the tie pin back in its box and put it away carefully.

``By the way, Del-chan---you said you had something urgent come up that day\dots\ was everything okay?''

Wednesday. My breath caught, like someone had grabbed me from behind.

\textit{I had to keep it secret that Hijiri and I had gone to the library together. I could say my little sister had a fever or something, but Mizasaki's younger brother went to the same middle school as Asahi, so the lie could get exposed---and besides, someone might have seen me heading to the library with Hijiri. I should've come up with an excuse in advance, but in the end, no good lie came to mind.}

``Yeah, Wednesday was---''

Before I could finish, Kannabi cleared her throat and cut in.

``Actually, I'm the one who gave him a fake excuse to go home early. I thought that way, the three of us might be able to choose a present.''

``Wait, seriously? That's a huge help.''

``\dots So there really is such a thing as a good lie.''

When I blurted out something half-baked, Kannabi grinned.

``I've decided I won't tell bad lies.''

Thanks to Kannabi's help, I was able to keep my promise to Mikage.

It might've been a little lacking in tact, but when Kannabi got up to go to the bathroom, I followed along, saying, ``I'll show you where it is.''

``Going together, huh.''

``Sorry\dots\ Thanks. About Wednesday.''

``It's fine. If you want to talk about why, my curiosity started it.''

I had nothing to say back. Kannabi glanced at me, then continued.

``So it really did turn into something big?''

``\dots I can't really say.''

``I see.''

After we walked a bit, Kannabi said,

``When you have to lie, it helps to use people.''

``What do you mean?''

``Make someone an accomplice. Create a situation where someone becomes your accomplice---or agrees to be. The more you try to cover things up alone, the more likely the secret you're hiding with that lie is to get found out.''

``What am I supposed to do when it's just the two of us talking like this?''

``Tell the lie the other person wants to believe, and make them your accomplice.''

``That's not something you can just say casually.''

The public restroom came into sight. It was split by gender, so we couldn't keep talking.

Kannabi stopped there and tapped me in the chest.

``I'll help too. So if you're going to act, then act the part---and keep acting all the way to the end.''

After Golden Week ended, on Tuesday after school, I was called to Sansetsuto after club.

This was the second time I'd been invited into a private room at this café, right when the sunset glare was at its strongest. Last time it had only been Hongo-senpai and Mikage Aya, but this time Mikage-senpai and Hijiri were there too.

An antique-style private room overlooking the sea. Hijiri and I sat beside Mikage, facing two third-years. The Physics Club captain and the Chemistry Club captain. At the same time, they were Tsunanagai High School's student council president and vice president.

A staff member carried the café's standard Sansetsuto blend to each of us. Even the soft fragrance drifting through the air couldn't erase the tension hanging over the room.

``First, as a student at Tsunanagai High School, I want to thank the two of you.''

Mikage-senpai opened the meeting. I'd met him before during new member recruitment, and just like that first impression, he was a refreshingly wholesome, good-looking upperclassman---those smile lines at the corners of his eyes only made him seem kinder.

``Thank you for exposing the wrongdoing that could've cost lives. And thank you for putting Shimomura-senpai's lingering regret to rest. Those are both things we couldn't do. I'm truly grateful.''

``N-no\dots\ it's not---''

As I bowed my head, Hijiri stayed composed at my side, not moving an inch. Hongo-senpai cast Hijiri a wary look. Mikage-senpai gave her shoulder a light pat, then said,

``I'll get straight to it. From here on out, this is a report on the cleanup afterward---and a meeting for the sake of what comes next.''

And then he took a long gulp of coffee.

``To be clear about my attitude upfront, I'm not here to scold you. So I'll get the hypothetical nagging out of the way first. If you'd come to consult us sooner, we could've settled this more amicably. If you'd relied on us, we could've helped.''

The coffee I'd never gotten around to sipping slowly cooled in front of me.

``What you two did was like digging up an unexploded bomb and hurling it into Shinju Bay. The documents Shimomura-senpai left behind are jet-black enough that it wouldn't be surprising if a few bureaucrats vanished because of them. What kind of first-year high schooler pushes something that dangerous straight at the prefectural governor?''

After letting out a sigh of exasperation, Mikage-senpai smiled.

``But you handled it so well it blew past anything we expected. I mean---who thinks you'd meet the governor the day after you go to city hall? Overall, I can't exactly praise your methods, but I'm not going to blame you for what you did. From here on, let's have a constructive discussion.''

Mikage-senpai gestured to my coffee. I dipped my head slightly and took a sip. It tasted more bitter than usual, but the aftertaste was lightly sweet. \textit{It seemed Mikage-senpai and the others were on our side.}

Beside me, just as my tension loosened a little, Hijiri pressed his lips together and stared straight at the upperclassmen. \textit{He still looked like he meant to confront them, and it made unease well up in me.}

``First, the megasolar issue. They're framing it as a city coordination mistake, and it seems construction will immediately proceed only on the sections that pose a landslide risk. Don't dig too much into the money side. I'll just say it looks like it'll be settled in a very gray way.''

Hijiri's eyebrow twitched. ``A gray way'' must've bothered him.

``And of course, the CHOSEI Group is extremely angry at our school, but that, too, will likely be squared away somewhere very gray. For now, you two can relax.''

I nodded. But Hijiri didn't.

``Looks like you've got a question, Hijiri-kun,'' Mikage-senpai said.

Hijiri immediately spoke.

``Until one point is made clear, I can't trust you.''

``Oh? Let's hear it.''

``In the past few days, I've looked thoroughly into the CHOSEI Group that built the megasolar facility. And something astonishing came to light.''

Hijiri pulled out an A4 sheet and set it on the table.

``The CHOSEI Group funds all sorts of places, strengthening its influence. Tsunazuna Shrine, which was running short on money. Senzawataku-so, which was on the verge of bankruptcy because of an infectious disease. They were able to develop the forest that was a forbidden zone, and they were able to renovate Senzawataku-so's gym and wipe out the place name---thanks to that funding.''

Hijiri spoke as he pointed to the upper half of the document, then slid his finger down to the lower half.

``And that kind of money is flowing into Tsunanagai High School, too.''

The two third-years shifted slightly.

``The Tsunanagai High School alumni association has abundant funds. Seventy percent of it came from the CHOSEI Group. The system for scouting top-performing students is funded by those donations. Even the dorm for out-of-prefecture students was built by a contractor from the CHOSEI Group.''

I was stunned. \textit{So that was it.}

\textit{I remembered that luxurious dorm. The out-of-prefecture students who lived there had their tuition fully covered, received a special stipend of 80,000 yen a month, and even had food and utilities paid by the school. I'd always wondered where that kind of money came from. I never imagined the same group that had forced through that megasolar construction was supporting it.}

\textit{And if the out-of-prefecture students' food expenses came from CHOSEI Group donations, then even that apple pie I'd eaten had been paid with dirty money.}

Glancing at me as I hesitated, Mikage-senpai nodded calmly.

``You did your homework.''

``In other words---especially you, Hongo-senpai, as an out-of-prefecture student---you're benefiting from that group's money. Do you understand what that means?''

Hongo-senpai kept sipping her coffee as if nothing bothered her. Mikage-senpai said,

``So you're saying we---or this school---are at the mercy of a corrupt company.''

``Otherwise, there's no way to explain what happened ten years ago. Shimomura-senpai in the Biology Club uncovered evidence of the megasolar construction's illegality. And yet, for some reason, it got buried. And the reason you're taking such a gray stance now---couldn't that also be influenced by the money involved?''

At Hijiri's accusation, a sharp silence fell over us.

``Alright,'' Mikage-senpai, folding his arms. ``Where do I even start?''

To start with, the CHOSEI Group and Tsunanagai High School go back decades. The group's representative is an old bastard named Tsurio, and he's one of our alumni. The system for scouting two students from outside the prefecture each year, and the system where alumni companies invest through the alumni association---he built all of it.

``\dots Invest?''

I couldn't help interrupting.

``So by donating to the school, they get something in return?''

``Right. They call it a donation, but in reality it's an investment. This is a high school that gathers the most talented students in the prefecture and brings in exceptional talent from all over the country. It's a treasure trove of human capital and connections. The amount of money they put in is peanuts. If you make the school owe you, the future returns are immeasurable. It's a low-risk, high-return investment.''

``If you know they're the wrong kind of people, then whether it's investment or donation, you should refuse it and cut ties.''

Hijiri pressed on without backing down.

``I think so too. But it seems they couldn't. They kept feeding the school, fattening it up little by little, until it couldn't keep going without their money. If the primary source dries up, then the out-of-prefecture scouting system, the generous activity support---everything---has to be abandoned.''

``Then abandon it.''

Mikage-senpai exchanged a glance with Hongo-senpai beside him. Hongo-senpai gave a small shake of her head.

``To tell you the truth, thanks to you two, it looks like we're going to abandon it.''

As Mikage-senpai sighed, Hongo-senpai smoothly picked up where he left off.

``The CHOSEI Group's financial support is obviously gone. Clean slate. And they'll probably put pressure on the other donors, too. Starting next year, donations won't just drop by seventy percent---more like ninety percent, I'd guess?''

Even Hijiri couldn't bring himself to say ``good'' in front of Hongo-senpai, an out-of-prefecture student.

Because what we'd done meant the alumni donations would drop to one-tenth.

Just the special stipend paid to the out-of-prefecture students was 80,000 yen a month---two students per grade---so by simple math, that was 5.76 million yen a year. And I couldn't even begin to imagine what the total would be once you added everything else.

``I'll say it again: I'm not blaming you for that outcome. Nagisa and I had been trying to cut ties as soon as we could. It just happened---oops---to happen a bit suddenly. Frankly, I was sick of letting them do whatever they wanted.''

Hijiri's expression stayed hard.

``So you admit it. That Tsunanagai High School's independence and self-governance were being threatened by CHOSEI Group donations---and you, as student council president, acknowledge that.''

``Yeah. I acknowledge it.''

Hijiri looked like he was about to say something, but Hongo-senpai stopped him as if she'd read him already.

``Let me explain what happened. I can't tell you everything, obviously---so I'll stick to what's relevant to this incident.''

After taking a sip of coffee, Hongo-senpai continued.

``First---Carson-senpai didn't go to America because she wanted to. She started an opposition movement against the megasolar project, made Tsurio furious, and got put through hell. The kind of hell where she couldn't stay in Japan. I can't say the specifics---because they're that bad.''

\textit{I'll do what I couldn't do.} Shimomura-senpai's note flashed through my mind.

The senpai who'd tried to do what we did ten years ago had been driven so far she had no choice but to leave the country. All because she tried to protect the flying-squirrel forest.

``And I think the reason the Biology Club was on the verge of collapsing was Tsurio's fault, too. For the past few years, nasty rumors were going around about the Biology Club. Like the timing was perfect---right when the activity restrictions started---people began spreading things like, `It's a trash club that can't do anything but take care of animals,' or `They're abusing animals.' Groundless slander, spreading everywhere.''

My thoughts stalled. \textit{No way---that, too?}

``\dots You think the source of that slander was the CHOSEI Group?''

``No proof. Not even Darling could pinpoint where rumors that old began. But who else would even have a motive to do that? It'd be that old bastard Tsurio, who's been wary of the Biology Club ever since the megasolar thing.''

``Darling'' was probably the person sitting beside her---Mikage Akifumi-senpai.

He let out a low, irritated sound.

``And when we decided to hold a Biology Club training camp again this year for the first time in a while, there was mysterious pressure from the teachers, too. Delta-kun, you remember that, don't you?''

He was right.

``You mean when they told us to make it one night instead of two?''

``Yeah. It's not like I wanted to be mean. They told us to cancel it, and I negotiated---`Then can we do one night?'---and barely got approval. We got lucky and managed to do it exactly how we wanted, thanks to the vice-principal.''

``Even on a bright, beautiful stage, what's behind the curtain is usually dark and filthy. I want you to understand this: the peaceful school life you see on the surface is something the teachers and student council protected by getting their hands covered in mud.''

As Mikage-senpai finished that line, the room dimmed all at once.
The setting sun had slipped behind the forest.

``Alright. I think we've shared what we needed to share. Lastly, I want to talk about what happens next.''

He watched the evening view beyond the wide window for a moment, then spoke---reluctant, as if he didn't want to say it.

``I told you this would be settled in a gray way, and I want you two to know what that means. In simple terms: it's going to be as if the CHOSEI Group never did anything improper with the megasolar project. It's being wrapped up as a city mistake---end of story.''

Hijiri's chair scraped loudly as he shifted.
